- **Counter-identification fails** when an alternative-self is presented (Ultimatum). The defense requires the rejected figure to remain external; an internal version of the rejected figure has nowhere to be put.
- **Splitting fails** when the binary is occupied by a beloved (Miles in the mask). The category cannot hold a person who is in both bins simultaneously.
- **Displacement fails** when the legitimate target is removed (Spider-Man is revealed to be Miles; the displacement target collapses into the love object).
- **Sublimation fails** when the sublimating structure is damaged (Rio's death; suspension from the force in some arcs).
- **Suppression fails** when the suppressed material is forced into the room by external event (Aaron's reappearance, the Ultimatum doppelganger, the reveal).

The Bendis run is, in some sense, the systematic stress-testing of each of Jefferson's defenses against a tailored adversary. He survives all of them, but the survival is structural — the underlying counter-identification scaffolding holds — not transformational. He does not develop new defenses; he keeps the old ones and adds *tolerance* on top.

---

## 6.7 Positive Compensatory Mechanisms

### 6.7.1 The Marriage as Co-Regulator

Rio functions, across the entire canon, as Jefferson's external affect regulator. She names what he cannot name, sits with what he cannot sit with, and softens what he cannot soften. The marriage is not symmetrical in this respect — he provides her with stability and protection; she provides him with the metabolizing function for affect his own architecture cannot perform. The marriage works because the asymmetry is mutual and acknowledged. Her death exposes how much defensive labor she was doing; her resurrection in the merged 616 timeline restores the co-regulation but the file should note that the dependency is now visible to him in a way it was not before.

### 6.7.2 The Badge as External Scaffold

The uniform, the precinct, the chain of command, the codified rules — these constitute an external scaffold on which his internal identity rests. The scaffold is load-bearing. Suspension from duty (which occurs in several arcs) produces visible regression: increased irritability, longer silences, more rigid household pronouncements. The scaffold is not the man, but it holds the man up.

### 6.7.3 Brooklyn Embeddedness

Decades of community ties function as a continuous external attestation of identity. Neighbors know him, the bodega owners know him, the schools know him. This dense network makes regression difficult (too many witnesses to the chosen self) and makes recovery from rupture easier (the network catches him).

### 6.7.4 Fatherhood as Generative Repair

Each act of parenting Miles is, at the unconscious level, a repair of the paternal failure he experienced. The repair is not perfect (he reproduces some of the rigidity he probably received) but it is genuine, and the generative dimension — the active making of a different father — is itself a compensatory mechanism that absorbs and metabolizes the original wound.

### 6.7.5 The Capacity to Stay in the Room

The most hard-won compensatory mechanism, developed across the Ahmed and Ziglar runs: the ability to remain physically and relationally present with material he cannot fully accept. He does not endorse the masked life; he stays in the room with the masked son. This is not a defense — it is the *renunciation* of his most characteristic defense (rupture) in favor of tolerated dissonance. It is the single most significant developmental achievement in the file.

---

## 6.8 Negative Compensatory Mechanisms

### 6.8.1 Categorical Moralism as Substitute for Grief Work

The blanket condemnation of vigilantism is, structurally, a way of not grieving Aaron and not grieving Rio. The moral certitude provides a continuous low-grade engagement with the trauma material that prevents it from being fully processed. He stays angry so he does not have to stay sad.

### 6.8.2 Rupture-as-Regulation

The willingness to sever a relationship rather than tolerate the affect it produces is a maladaptive compensatory pattern. It worked once — with Aaron — and the success of that severance has made it the template for crisis management. The Miles estrangement is the same move applied to a relationship where it should not have been applied. He has learned, painfully and incompletely, to not run the move again, but it remains in the repertoire and can re-emerge under sufficient load.

### 6.8.3 Over-Control as Identity

The same over-control that produces his reliability also produces his brittleness. He cannot relax fully without feeling that he is sliding toward the unchosen self. This means that some categories of experience — spontaneity, play, vulnerability with non-Rio adults, the ordinary looseness of a man at rest — are unavailable to him. The compensatory cost of his identity stability is the bandwidth of his experience.

### 6.8.4 Verbal Withholding

He under-praises. He under-affirms. The doorway monologue in the film canon is structurally important precisely because the words are so rare — he can only deliver them through a barrier, believing he is not heard. The compensatory cost to Miles is high: Miles spends years uncertain of his father's approval not because the approval is absent but because the channel through which it would travel is closed. Jefferson knows this and cannot fully open the channel.

### 6


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE: JEFFERSON DAVIS / MORALES
## Decade-by-Decade Clinical Mapping, c. Childhood–Present

The following section traces the subject's psychological organization across roughly five developmental epochs, using the canonical published record (Bendis 2011–2018, Ahmed 2018–2022, Ziglar 2022–present, and the *Spider-Verse* film/PS-game adaptations) as the evidentiary base. Frameworks invoked: Bowlby/Main attachment theory; Kernberg's structural model of personality organization; McWilliams's nomenclature of defensive style; Linehan's biosocial/affect-regulation model; Beck's schema theory; Bromberg on dissociation and self-states; the Allen/Fonagy mentalization frame; and the PTSD/Prolonged Grief criteria of DSM-5-TR. The diagnostic conclusions in §4 of the shared workup are treated as established; the work here is to show *how* those structures formed, hardened, fractured, and were partially repaired across time.

---

## EPOCH I — Childhood (roughly ages 0–12; Brooklyn, late 1960s–1970s in the Ultimate timeline / modernized to 1980s–90s in film canon)

**Affect regulation.** The earliest inferable layer. Jefferson grows up in a household where his father is, by his own retrospective testimony in *Miles Morales: Ultimate Spider-Man* #6–7 and the prison-visit conversations, intermittently abusive, intermittently absent, and never a reliable container for the child's distress. The functional caregiver in many flashback panels is Aaron — older brother as proto-parent — which is the structural setup Bowlby would expect to produce a *role-reversed* or *parentified* younger sibling, except here the dynamic is inverted: Jefferson is *cared for* by a sibling who is himself dysregulated. The child therefore learns two things in parallel: (a) that affect is regulated externally, by the brother's presence, and (b) that the regulator is himself unsafe.

The likely consequence — and one consistent with the adult presentation — is the early development of an **over-controlled coping style** (Chapman & Gross's terminology): the child throttles affect at source because the environment cannot be trusted to metabolize it. Crying, fear, want — all suppressed. What gets through is hypervigilant scanning and a precocious moralism (a child who tells himself stories about *who is good* and *who is bad* because the adults around him will not).

**Cognitive style.** Early concrete-operational rigidity, locked in by environmental necessity. The child needs categorical rules ("Dad is dangerous when he drinks," "Aaron is safe when he is calm") to navigate a household with unpredictable contingencies. This is the seed of the categorical, rule-bound cognition that dominates the adult.

**Self-concept.** Fragmentary and largely defined by negation. The boy knows what he does *not* want to be — does not want to be hit, does not want to be afraid, does not want to be his father — long before he knows what he *is*. This is the pre-history of the adult's identity organized around a single redemptive act.

**Attachment classification at this stage.** Most consistent with **disorganized/insecure-avoidant**, the disorganization driven by the father (frightening/frightened caregiver), the avoidant overlay driven by the strategy that worked (suppress, present-as-okay, do not approach the unsafe adult).

---

## EPOCH II — Adolescence and Young Adulthood (roughly ages 13–22; the "running with Aaron" period)

This is the **delinquency phase** that Bendis stages across the *Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* #3–4 flashbacks and elaborates in the *Miles Morales* prison-visit dialogue. Jefferson and Aaron are burglars, then escalating. The published record is careful to keep Jefferson at the lower end of the spectrum — property crime, presence at events, never the principal violent actor — but he is unambiguously a participant.

**Affect regulation.** Paradoxically *better* during this period than in childhood, for a counter-intuitive reason: criminal activity with Aaron provides three things the household never did — *predictable arousal regulation* (the rush-and-recovery cycle of a job), *belonging* (a dyad with shared purpose), and *competence* (he is good at it). The over-controlled child gets a sanctioned outlet for arousal. This is the phase that, in the absence of the rupture, would have hardened into ASPD trajectory. It did not, and the reason is diagnostically important: the affect that the criminal life *could not* metabolize was guilt. Aaron does not feel it; Jefferson does. The guilt is the proto-symptom of the moral structure that will later become his identity.

**Cognitive style.** Splitting begins to crystallize as a deliberate cognitive operation, not just an inherited childhood schema. Aaron's worldview — *us against the world, the rules are for suckers* — is internalized briefly and then becomes the object Jefferson will define himself against. The splitting in the adult is in some sense a *learned tool*, picked up from a brother who used it for the opposite purpose.

**Self-concept.** Unstable. The young man is trying on the *Aaron identity* as a hand-me-down. Bendis writes him in flashback with a slouched posture, a borrowed swagger that does not sit right — physical tells of a self that is rented rather than owned.

**The conversion event.** Canon places the rupture in a specific incident — Aaron's escalation to violence Jefferson refuses to follow — after which Jefferson walks into a precinct. Clinically this is a **quantum change** event in William Miller's sense: sudden, vivid, enduring, organized around a moral insight rather than gradual behavioral shaping. Quantum changes have a known signature: they reorganize identity around a single act of decision and tend to leave the convert with a *brittle but powerful* new structure. They are not therapy; they do not process the underlying material; they wall it off. Everything about Jefferson's adult organization is consistent with this etiology.

**Attachment classification at this stage.** The Aaron dyad functions as an **insecure-preoccupied** sibling attachment — intense, ambivalent, the entire emotional weight loaded onto one figure. The rupture is therefore not a clean walk-out; it is the amputation of his primary attachment object. The grief that will surface twenty years later when Aaron dies has its root here.

---

## EPOCH III — Early Adulthood and Marriage (roughly ages 22–32; the academy, beat cop years, courtship and marriage to Rio, birth of Miles)

**Affect regulation.** The badge functions exactly as Winnicott's *holding environment* and Bion's *container* would predict for a man whose internal structure cannot hold its own contents. The uniform externalizes the over-control he learned in childhood and the structure he chose in conversion. Procedure, chain of command, the radio, the partner — all of it offloads affect-regulation onto an institution. This is, on net, *adaptive*: it allows him to function at a high level without the symptomatic burden that an unscaffolded man with his history would carry.

Marriage to Rio adds the second pillar. Rio is, in every panel Bendis and Pichelli give us, the emotionally fluent one — quick to laugh, quick to express, culturally rooted in a Puerto Rican household where affect is *spoken*. She is, in technical terms, his **affect-regulation collaborator**: she does the emotional metabolizing he cannot. The marriage is a functional complementarity, not a symmetry. He provides the floor; she provides the air.

**Cognitive style.** The categorical rigidity of the child becomes the *proceduralism* of the adult cop. This is a sublimation in the classical sense — the same cognitive machinery, redirected from defensive scanning to legitimate professional use. He is, by all the published evidence, a *good* cop in the craft sense: observant, rule-following, not corrupt, not brutal. The same traits that made him a competent burglar (pattern recognition, threat assessment, planning) now make him a competent patrolman.

**Self-concept.** Consolidates around "I am the man who walked away." This becomes the load-bearing self-statement. Crucially, it is **continuously re-earned through conduct** — Jefferson cannot rest in the identity, because the identity is defined by an act, and acts must be repeated. This produces the chronic self-monitoring and the over-conscientiousness that read at trait level as subclinical OCPD.

**Attachment classification at this stage.** Movement toward **earned security**. The marriage is the engine. The Main/Hesse construct of earned-secure attachment — adults with insecure childhood histories who, via a corrective adult relationship, achieve coherent autobiographical narrative and secure functioning — fits Jefferson cleanly in this epoch. Note the qualifier: *earned*. It is held in place by Rio. It is not yet self-sustaining.

---

## EPOCH IV — Mid-Adulthood / Parenting Years (roughly ages 32–45; Miles's childhood through age 13, the spider-bite, the early Ultimate run)

This is the period of greatest apparent stability and greatest accumulating strain. The exterior is composed; the interior is loading.

**Affect regulation.** Holds, but with rising baseline tension. The arrival of fatherhood reactivates dormant material — every developmental milestone of Miles's is also an unconscious checkpoint against Jefferson's own childhood and his brother's. He is hyper-attuned to any sign that Miles is drifting toward Aaron's pattern. Bendis stages this directly in *Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* #3–4 — Jefferson's reaction to Aaron's reappearance is volcanic and disproportionate, because Aaron's presence is a *direct contagion vector* to the son. The affect that leaks here is anger, never sadness, and never about Jefferson — always framed as protection.

**Cognitive style.** The blanket category of "people in masks" begins to form as a *cognitive economy*. He does not have the bandwidth, given the affect load, to differentiate types of mask-wearers; they are collapsed into one threat class. This is a textbook **Beckian overgeneralization schema** — a single rule applied across a category to spare the cognitive system the cost of case-by-case appraisal. It is efficient and it is wrong, and the wrongness is structurally necessary to him.

**Self-concept.** Begins to show the first hairline fractures. Aaron's reappearances function as *return of the repressed* — each one forces Jefferson to re-meet the version of himself he amputated. He responds with reaction-formation intensity (loud condemnation, exclusion), which is, in McWilliams's framework, the signature defense of someone whose identity rests on the opposite of what is being shown to him.

**Parenting style.** Authoritative in the Baumrind sense, but skewed toward the *demanding* axis over the *responsive* axis. High expectations, clear rules, visible love expressed through provision and presence rather than verbal affirmation. He under-praises and over-corrects, as already noted. This is the parenting style of a man who is terrified of his son's freedom and who knows enough to not say so directly.

**Attachment with Miles at this stage.** Secure-anxious-protective. The anxiety is not about the child's worth; it is about the world's safety and the family's legacy.

---

## EPOCH V — Late Mid-Adulthood / The Trauma Years (roughly ages 45–50; Aaron's death, the Venom attack, Rio's death, the reveal and estrangement)

The pillars come down in sequence.

**Aaron's death (*Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* #15).** Jefferson grieves a brother he had publicly disowned, without knowing his son was the proximate cause. This is the canonical setup for **Prolonged Grief Disorder** — a death that cannot be mourned cleanly because the relationship was not whole at the time of loss. Symptoms manifest indirectly: increased rigidity, a hardening of the anti-mask stance (Aaron died in a *mask*), and a quiet, unspoken anniversary reactivity that Bendis tracks in occasional silent panels.

**The Venom attack and Rio's death (*Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* #22).** Criterion A trauma. The clinical picture from this point forward includes intrusive imagery, physiological reactivity to mask-cued stimuli, sleep disruption, irritability, hypervigilance — the full PTSD symptom complex (DSM-5-TR Criteria B–E), as outlined in §4. The affect-regulation collaborator is dead. The earned-secure attachment loses its scaffold. He reverts, under load, toward the *avoidant-disorganized* baseline of childhood — colder, more procedural, longer hours at work, less in the house, less in himself.

**Cognitive style during this period.** Catastrophic narrowing. The overgeneralization schema goes from defensive convenience to operational doctrine. *Masks kill wives.* The grief requires an external agent; Spider-Man becomes the agent; the category is sealed. Mentalization — his capacity to hold others' minds in mind — degrades sharply during the acute period. He loses, temporarily, the ability to imagine that the masked figure who failed to save Rio was also a frightened person, possibly his son.

**The reveal and estrangement (*Spider-Man* #234–240).** When Miles reveals his identity, Jefferson's response is the **expel-then-revise** pattern that §3 of the workup identifies as diagnostic. He cannot integrate the data in real time, so he ejects the relationship to preserve the schema. This is, in Bromberg's terms, a **dissociative self-state shift** — the *grieving cop who hates masks* state and the *father who loves his son* state cannot coexist in the same moment, so one is foregrounded at the cost of the other. The estrangement is the period during which those states are walled off from each other. Repair requires their gradual reintegration.

**Self-concept during this period.** Threatened at the foundation. The "I am the man who walked away" statement no longer holds, because the man he walked from has reappeared inside his own son. He is, briefly, *no one* — and the symptomatic load of that no-one period is what shows up as withdrawal, terse speech, the badge as the only remaining anchor.

---

## EPOCH VI — Reconciliation and Integration (roughly ages 50+; late Bendis, Ahmed, Ziglar, and the film canon's parallel rendering)

The arc here is not transformation. It is, as §5 of the workup correctly identifies, *tolerance* — a hard-won capacity to remain in proximity to what he cannot endorse.

**Affect regulation.** Rebuilds, with Rio's resurrection in the merged 616 timeline restoring the collaborator function but never restoring the pre-trauma baseline. He runs hotter now; the irritability threshold is lower; the recovery from rupture is faster but the rupture is closer to the surface. This is the typical post-traumatic equilibrium: function restored, reactivity elevated, repair skills sharpened by necessity.

**Cognitive style.** The blanket category begins, slowly, to admit exceptions. Miles is the first exception, and his presence as a *good masked figure who is also my son* is the wedge that eventually pries the category open enough to admit others. By the Ahmed run he is shown tolerating — barely, with visible strain — the presence of other Spider-people in his house. He does not become open-minded; he becomes *case-by-case*, which for a man of his cognitive style is an enormous shift.

**The Ultimatum confrontation (Ahmed run).** Diagnostically the most important late-period event. Jefferson meets the Earth-1610 version of himself — the man he would have been if Rio had not anchored him, if the trauma had hit a self without the marriage to hold it. The look the published record gives him in those panels is *recognition*, not horror — he knows the man on sight, because the man is the unintegrated remainder he has been managing his whole adult life. This is, in Jungian terms, a direct shadow encounter, and it does not destroy him. That it does not is the proof of the integration work the previous decade has done.

**Self-concept at the late stage.** Restructures from "I am the man who walked away" to something closer to "I am the man who keeps choosing." The shift is from a single past act to an ongoing practice — which is, developmentally, a more mature self-organization. Erikson's *generativity vs. stagnation* resolves on the generative side: he is, at this stage, oriented toward what he is *building* (his son, his marriage, the small Brooklyn community he tends) rather than what he *escaped*.

**Attachment at the late stage.** Earned-secure, no longer wholly dependent on Rio as the sole scaffold. The capacity to *initiate repair*, to *stay in the room*, to *speak love through the door* even when he believes it will not be heard — all of these are markers of internalized security that does not require the partner's constant active regulation. He is, for the first time in the published record, his own container.

---

## CROSS-EPOCH SYNTHESIS

What changes across the decades is the *location* of his regulation: external (sibling) → externalized but absent (delinquent dyad) → institutional (badge) + relational (marriage) → catastrophically destabilized (trauma) → reconstituted on a more internal axis (late period). What does not change is the underlying machinery: over-controlled affect, categorical cognition, identity organized around moral decision, and love expressed through act rather than statement. The arc is not a man becoming someone else. It is a man learning, slowly and at great cost, to hold more of himself at once.

The clinically operative datum, across every epoch, is this: Jefferson Davis's psychology is the psychology of a man who made one large decision in his early twenties and has been paying the maintenance costs on it ever since. The decision was sound. The costs are real. The late-period maturity is the gradual discovery that the decision can be *renewed* rather than *defended* — and that renewal is cheaper, over time, than defense.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL
## Subject: Davis, Jefferson (a.k.a. Morales, Jefferson)
### File Section 4 — Clinical Formulation, Diagnostic Workup, Longitudinal Course, Differential Exclusions

---

## 4.0 Framing and Method

This section converts the longitudinal behavioral record (1980s adolescence in Brooklyn through the present-tense post-*Secret Wars*/integrated-616 era and parallel film-canon timeline) into formal psychiatric language. It uses DSM-5-TR criterion structure as the primary scaffold, with ICD-11 cross-references where the latter captures the presentation more cleanly (notably for Prolonged Grief and Complex PTSD). The subject has never, in any recorded continuity, presented for psychiatric care; there is no medication record, no chart, no inpatient or partial-hospital episode. Every diagnostic statement below is therefore derived from observable conduct, speech samples, dyadic and triadic interaction data, occupational record, and the somatic correlates documented in §2.

The clinical picture is *not* a single disorder. It is a layered presentation: a personality structure organized around rigid counter-identification, sitting atop a developmental trauma substrate, with two adult-onset Criterion-A events producing a chronic, moderate, sub-threshold-at-times trauma syndrome, intertwined with a textbook prolonged-grief reaction to a deliberately disowned sibling. The diagnostic art with Davis is *not* finding the disorder; it is correctly weighting how much of his presentation is illness versus how much is a well-defended, high-functioning, internalizing personality style doing exactly what it was constructed to do.

---

## 4.1 Primary Diagnosis

### **Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder, Chronic, Moderate Severity, With Predominant Anger/Externalizing Features**
*(DSM-5-TR 309.81 / ICD-11 6B40)*

This is the cleanest, best-supported diagnosis in the file. It is also the diagnosis Davis himself would most resist, because acknowledging it would require him to relinquish the moral framing of his anti-vigilante stance ("I am right about this") in favor of a clinical framing ("I am injured, and my conviction is partly a symptom").

**Criterion A — Stressor.** Two qualifying events, each independently sufficient:
1. The symbiote/Venom attack on the Morales home (*Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* #22, and the surrounding arc): direct exposure to a life-threatening event involving actual or threatened death and serious injury, including witnessing the grievous wounding and death of his spouse. This event satisfies A.1 (direct experience), A.2 (witnessing in person), and A.3 (learning of, in the immediate sense, the death of a close family member through violent means) simultaneously — an unusually saturated Criterion A presentation.
2. Repeated line-of-duty exposure across a multi-decade NYPD career, including the HYDRA-occupied-NYC arc (resistance-cell activity, *Spider-Man* #6–10 era), Cataclysm-period civil collapse, and chronic exposure to violent crime scenes consistent with patrol/sergeant duty in a high-call-volume precinct. This produces the cumulative-exposure pattern documented in first-responder literature and qualifies independently under DSM-5-TR Criterion A.4 (repeated or extreme exposure to aversive details).

**Criterion B — Intrusion (≥1 required; subject meets 3).**
- B.2 (recurrent distressing dreams): not directly depicted but inferable from the episodic insomnia post-Rio.
- B.3 (dissociative reactions): the "stare" sequences when confronted with the Ultimatum doppelganger (Ahmed run) function as brief depersonalization-adjacent episodes — Davis goes still, affect flattens, speech becomes monosyllabic. This is not catatonic; it is a peri-traumatic dissociative micro-episode triggered by an identity-threatening stimulus.
- B.4 (intense or prolonged psychological distress at cues): consistently triggered by masked figures, by Aaron-coded stimuli (the Prowler iconography), by mention of Spider-Man during the post-Rio period.
- B.5 (marked physiological reactivity): jaw-set, shoulder-rise, hand-to-belt approach, vocal-register drop — these are documented across multiple writers and consistent enough to be considered a stable somatic response pattern (cross-reference §6 behavioral micro-patterns).

**Criterion C — Avoidance (≥1 required; subject meets both).**
- C.1 (avoidance of internal reminders): refusal to speak about Aaron post-disownment; the conversation in the *Miles Morales: Ultimate Spider-Man* #6–7 prison sequence shows the *effort* required to override this avoidance, which is itself diagnostic.
- C.2 (avoidance of external reminders): refusal to discuss Spider-Man with Miles during the early reveal aftermath, physical leaving-the-room behavior, the documented year-plus period of reduced household conversation.

**Criterion D — Negative alterations in cognition and mood (≥2 required; subject meets 4).**
- D.2 (persistent and exaggerated negative beliefs): "people in masks" as a totalizing moral category — heroes and villains collapsed into one indictment. This is the single most diagnostically loud symptom in the file because the cognitive distortion is *visible to the reader and invisible to the subject*.
- D.3 (distorted cognitions about cause/consequence leading to blame): blames Spider-Man for Rio's death despite the actual causal chain being the Venom symbiote and the broader vigilante ecology. The blame attribution is selective and trauma-shaped.
- D.4 (persistent negative emotional state): predominantly anger, with sub-currents of guilt and shame regarding Aaron.
- D.6 (feelings of detachment or estrangement): the rupture from Miles post-reveal; the long-standing emotional distance from peer officers despite respect.

**Criterion E — Alterations in arousal and reactivity (≥2 required; subject meets 4).**
- E.1 (irritable behavior and angry outbursts): the confrontations with Aaron, the badge-on-the-table moments, the door-slam reactions. Critically, these are *not* the modal Davis — they are episodic eruptions in an otherwise over-controlled presentation, which is itself a signature of internalizing-presentation PTSD.
- E.3 (hypervigilance): chronically scans rooms, knows exits, registers Miles's posture and clothing for tells; this is also occupational hygiene and the two are not separable.
- E.4 (exaggerated startle): documented at multiple points post-Venom incident.
- E.6 (sleep disturbance): situational insomnia during loss periods.

**Criteria F, G, H** (duration >1 month, clinically significant distress/impairment, not attributable to substance/medical) — all met. Impairment is concentrated in the parental dyad with Miles and, secondarily, in the marital recovery period; occupational function is preserved and arguably enhanced by the symptom complex (hypervigilance and irritability are operationally adaptive for patrol work, which is part of why the disorder is missable).

**Specifiers:**
- *With predominant anger/externalizing features* (not a formal DSM specifier, but a clinically useful descriptor): Davis's PTSD does not present as the modal civilian-trauma picture of withdrawal and numbing dominance; it presents as the first-responder/military-veteran variant in which anger is the lead affect and avoidance is enacted through interpersonal severance rather than agoraphobia or generalized withdrawal.
- *Chronic*: symptom course exceeds three months and has now run multi-year.
- Does **not** meet criteria for *With Dissociative Symptoms* specifier — the dissociative micro-episodes are too brief and stimulus-bound to qualify.

**Severity: Moderate.** Severe is reserved for presentations producing substantial occupational impairment, frank dissociation, or active suicidality, none of which are present. Mild understates the relational damage. Moderate captures it.

---

## 4.2 Co-Primary Diagnosis

### **Prolonged Grief Disorder**
*(DSM-5-TR 309.89 / ICD-11 6B42)*

Two grief objects: Aaron (primary, structurally unresolved across the entire published record) and Rio (acute, partially resolved by her resurrection in merged continuity but leaving residue).

**For Aaron:** The grief satisfies DSM-5-TR PGD criteria with unusual textbook precision *because* it was preceded by disownment. Standard mourning processes — reminiscence, integration of the ambivalent object, acceptance of the loss, gradual reorganization of self around the absence — cannot run on a relationship that the subject deliberately severed *before* death intervened. The pre-death severance freezes the relationship in its last conflicted state and prevents the normative oscillation between yearning and acceptance described in dual-process bereavement models.

Specific criteria met:
- Intense yearning/preoccupation: surfaces displaced as anger at Aaron-coded stimuli; surfaces directly in the *Miles Morales: Ultimate Spider-Man* #6–7 prison conversation and the brief sequences where Davis handles Aaron's effects.
- Identity disruption: he organized his entire adult identity around *not being his brother*, so the brother's death paradoxically destabilizes the identity (the negative pole of the dyad has gone silent).
- Marked sense of disbelief and emotional pain: registered as flat affect and jaw-tension rather than tears — culturally and characterologically congruent presentation.
- Avoidance of reminders.
- Intense loneliness specifically about the sibling slot (he never re-attaches to a brother figure).
- Feeling that life is meaningless without the deceased — does *not* meet. Davis's meaning structure (marriage, son, badge) is intact. This is partial PGD, not complete.

Duration well exceeds the 12-month threshold; symptoms are persistent and cause clinically significant interpersonal impairment (the displacement of grief-anger onto Miles's vigilantism is the operative mechanism of the estrangement arc).

**For Rio:** The Rio grief in the Ultimate continuity met acute grief criteria and was trending toward PGD when the merged-continuity resurrection short-circuited the process. The resurrection does not fully resolve the trauma — Davis retains the *embodied memory* of having lost her, and certain behaviors (the way he tracks her location, the way he insists on driving her to certain shifts, the documented increase in physical-proximity-seeking when she is in the same room) are residue. This is closer to a chronic adjustment reaction than to PGD in current form.

---

## 4.3 Trait-Level / Personality Findings

### **Obsessive-Compulsive Personality Traits, Subclinical**
*(would code, if disordered, as DSM-5-TR 301.4 / ICD-11 6D11.5)*

Davis displays four of the eight OCPD criteria at trait level:
- Preoccupation with rules, order, and organization (extends from job to household).
- Excessive devotion to work and productivity to the exclusion of leisure (modal coping move under stress is *more shifts*).
- Over-conscientious, scrupulous, and inflexible about morality (the defining feature).
- Rigidity and stubbornness.

He does **not** meet the perfectionism, hoarding, miserliness, or reluctance-to-delegate criteria with sufficient consistency to push trait into disorder. Critically, OCPD requires that the pattern cause clinically significant distress or impairment; Davis's traits are largely ego-syntonic and operationally beneficial. Subclinical only. The traits *amplify* the PTSD presentation (rigid moral cognition reinforces trauma-derived global negative beliefs) and *constrain* it (the same rigidity prevents disorganized spiraling).

### **Earned-Secure Attachment with Disorganized Activation Under Specific Stressors**

Attachment classification, derived from observed dyadic behavior: earned-secure with Rio; anxious-protective with Miles; disorganized-residual with Aaron (now collapsed into the grief). The "earned" qualifier matters — Davis did not begin with secure attachment; he constructed it through the marriage. Earned-secure individuals are more vulnerable than primary-secure individuals to attachment-relevant trauma, which is consistent with the severity of his reaction to Rio's death.

---

## 4.4 Comorbidity Mapping and Course

**Bidirectional reinforcement:** The PTSD and the PGD potentiate each other. The PTSD's negative cognition cluster ("masks make things worse") provides a cognitive container for the displaced Aaron-grief ("my brother chose masks and it killed him; my son chooses masks and it will kill him"). The PGD's avoidance feeds the PTSD's avoidance. Treating one without the other would, in any plausible clinical encounter, fail.

**OCPD traits as scaffold:** The trait structure provides the over-control that *prevents* the PTSD from presenting as the more disorganized, substance-involved, occupationally-collapsing variant common in his demographic and occupational cohort. This is why he looks high-functioning on the surface and why the disorder is so easy to miss.

**Course, longitudinal:**

- *Pre-rupture phase (adolescence, pre–police academy):* Subclinical conduct features tied to peer/sibling modeling; no evidence of true Conduct Disorder (insufficient breadth, terminated cleanly).
- *Conversion phase (academy through early marriage):* No active disorder; emergence of OCPD trait structure as identity scaffold.
- *Stable adult phase (early Miles childhood):* Baseline. Trait-level rigidity only.
- *First trauma layer (Aaron's reappearance, then death, then disownment-frozen grief):* Onset of PGD-spectrum symptoms, initially compensated.
- *Second trauma layer (Venom attack, Rio's death in Ultimate continuity):* Full PTSD onset, acute then chronic; PGD intensifies; estrangement from Miles follows the reveal.
- *Reintegration phase (Ahmed/Ziglar runs, merged continuity):* PTSD becomes chronic-moderate with reduced acute episodes; PGD partially metabolized for Rio (resurrection), persistent for Aaron; behavioral functioning returns to near-baseline with permanent residue in the parental relationship.
- *Current state:* Compensated chronic PTSD, partial PGD, stable OCPD traits, no acute risk. Functional in occupation, marriage, parenting — with the qualifier that "functional" here means "operating inside an identity-defended structure that the subject cannot examine without destabilizing."

**Risk profile:**
- Suicide risk: low at baseline, would elevate to moderate in a scenario involving (a) loss of Rio again with no resurrection mechanism, (b) loss of Miles, or (c) public exposure of his pre-academy criminal history in a way that collapses the redemptive identity. Protective factors: religious/community embeddedness (implied, Brooklyn-specific), the badge as identity anchor, the marriage.
- Violence risk: low in civilian contexts; appropriate-to-elevated in occupational context; *elevated specifically* in scenarios threatening Rio or Miles, where rule-bound restraint collapses into direct action. This is not pathological — it is the predictable behavior of a securely-attached protector — but it should be noted in any operational risk assessment.
- Substance risk: low. The *absence* of substance reliance in a man with this family history, this trauma load, and this occupation is statistically anomalous and clinically meaningful (see §2).

---

## 4.5 Differential Diagnosis — What He Is NOT, and Why

A rigorous differential is required because surface features of Davis's presentation can be misread into several incorrect diagnostic frames, each of which would distort understanding and (in a hypothetical clinical encounter) misdirect intervention.

### **Not Antisocial Personality Disorder.**
The youthful criminal history (burglaries with Aaron) is the only feature that points this direction, and it fails on every other criterion. ASPD requires a *pervasive pattern* of disregard for the rights of others *since age 15* and *continuing into adulthood*. Davis's delinquency terminated with a discrete moral reorganization in late adolescence/early adulthood, followed by decades of prosocial conduct, deep attachment capacity, sustained guilt and remorse, and a chosen vocation organized around the protection of others' rights. ASPD individuals do not typically demonstrate the capacity for reaction formation at the scale Davis demonstrates; the defense requires intact superego function, which is precisely what ASPD lacks. Rule-out: definitive.

### **Not Narcissistic Personality Disorder.**
The moral certainty and the categorical pronouncements can superficially mimic narcissistic grandiosity. They are not. NPD requires grandiose self-enhancement, need for admiration, lack of empathy. Davis's moralism is *defensive*, not self-enhancing — he derives no pleasure from being right and visibly hates the moments when his rightness costs him his son. He does not seek admiration; he seeks order. Empathic capacity is intact, frequently displayed (with Miles, with Rio, with neighborhood civilians, even — in restrained form — with suspects). The doorway monologue in film canon is dispositive: a narcissist does not deliver love through a barrier where he believes he will not be heard, because a narcissist's expressions of love are performances oriented toward an audience. Rule-out: definitive.

### **Not Borderline Personality Disorder.**
Splitting is present and was identified in §3 as a core defense. This is the diagnostic trap. BPD splitting is *pervasive across relationships and across time*, with rapid oscillation between idealization and devaluation of the *same* object. Davis's splitting is *categorical and stable*: masked vs. unmasked, badge vs. no-badge. He does not flip Rio between idealization and devaluation; he does not flip Miles. The categories are rigid, not labile. Identity is over-stable, not diffuse. There is no chronic emptiness, no abandonment-driven dysregulation outside the discrete trauma response, no self-harm, no impulsive self-damaging behaviors, no suicidality. The estrangement from Miles post-reveal looks superficially like BPD abandonment dynamics but is actually a trauma-driven schema-protection move — he severs to preserve the worldview, not to preempt being severed from. Rule-out: definitive.

### **Not Obsessive-Compulsive Personality Disorder (full disorder).**
Already addressed in §4.3 — trait-level only, ego-syntonic, no clinically significant impairment attributable to the traits themselves. Rule-out: definitive at disorder level; traits coded.

### **Not Obsessive-Compulsive Disorder.**
No ego-dystonic intrusive obsessions, no compulsive rituals oriented to neutralizing obsessions. The procedural rigidity is characterological, not symptom-driven. Rule-out: definitive.

### **Not Major Depressive Disorder, Recurrent.**
Depressive episodes are situational, tied to identifiable losses (Aaron, Rio), and resolve with restoration of stabilizing objects or with time. Baseline mood is restricted-but-engaged, not depressed. No anhedonia in stable periods, no neurovegetative symptoms outside acute loss windows, no recurrent endogenous-pattern episodes. The post-Rio period in Ultimate continuity reached threshold for a single Major Depressive Episode, situationally specified; it did not recur as an independent mood disorder. Rule-out: definitive for recurrent MDD; single episode, situational, in partial-to-full remission, is supportable as a historical diagnosis.

### **Not Persistent Depressive Disorder (Dysthymia).**
Restricted affect ≠ chronic depression. Davis's restricted affect is characterological and cultural, not a mood-disorder symptom. He has clearly observable positive affect in stable conditions (with Rio, in small Miles moments, in occupational mastery experiences). Rule-out: definitive.

### **Not Generalized Anxiety Disorder.**
Hypervigilance is trauma-derived and occupationally reinforced, not free-floating anxious apprehension across multiple life domains. He does not worry about finances, health, minor decisions, or social evaluation in the GAD pattern. His vigilance is narrowly focused on specific threat categories. Rule-out: definitive.

### **Not Adjustment Disorder.**
Considered for the post-Rio and post-reveal periods. Excluded because the symptom presentation in both cases meets the threshold for the specific disorders coded above (PTSD, PGD, situational MDE), and adjustment disorder is a residual category used only when criteria for the specific disorders are not met.

### **Not Acute Stress Disorder.**
Considered for the immediate post-Venom-attack window. Likely met criteria during that window; superseded by the chronic PTSD coding as the symptom complex exceeded one month.

### **Not Complex PTSD (ICD-11).**
This is the *closest near-miss* and deserves explicit treatment. C-PTSD requires the core PTSD symptoms plus persistent disturbances in self-organization across three domains: affect dysregulation, negative self-concept, and interpersonal disturbance. Davis has affect dysregulation (the anger eruptions) and interpersonal disturbance (the rupture pattern) but does *not* have the persistent negative self-concept characteristic of C-PTSD — his self-concept is, if anything, over-positive in its moral-redemptive framing ("I am the man who walked away"). The developmental adversity in his history is real but did not produce the pervasive self-organization disturbances C-PTSD requires; it produced a *defended* self-organization. Rule-out: differential considered, classification retained as standard PTSD.

### **Not Substance Use Disorder, any class.**
Affirmatively absent. Social alcohol use only across the entire published record. Diagnostically meaningful in context (see §2 and §4.4 risk profile).

### **Not a Psychotic-Spectrum Disorder.**
No history of psychotic symptoms, thought disorder, or reality-testing impairment. The categorical thinking about masked figures is overvalued ideation in the trauma-derived sense, not delusion. Reality testing intact across the record. Rule-out: definitive.

### **Not a Neurodevelopmental Disorder.**
No evidence of ADHD, ASD, or learning-disability features. Intellectual functioning average-to-above-average with strong pattern-recognition and verbal-reasoning components (Bendis writes him as articulate and reflective in private dialogue). The interpersonal restraint and parallel-activity preference can superficially read as ASD-adjacent in casual observation; it is characterological and trauma-shaped, not neurodevelopmental. Rule-out: definitive.

---

## 4.6 Etiological Synthesis

A four-layer model captures the full picture:

1. **Developmental substr


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS: JEFFERSON DAVIS (a.k.a. Jefferson Morales)

*A longitudinal catalog of micro-behavior, decision habits, somatic tells, and conditional responses, drawn across the full published record (Bendis, Ahmed, Ziglar; film canon; game canon) and indexed by state. This is the granular layer beneath the psychological workup — the things a surveillance officer would notice on day three of the watch, and the things a wife notices on year twenty.*

---

## I. BASELINE — THE MAN AT REST

There is no true rest state. Even at the kitchen table on a day off, the subject sits with his back to a wall and his chair angled so that the front door is in peripheral vision. This is so habitual it precedes the badge — it is the posture of a young man who used to listen for footfalls on a stairwell — and he is no longer aware he does it. When Rio moves a chair, he moves it back.

**Posture.** Squared shoulders, weight slightly forward, hands more often on his thighs than in his lap. He stands with feet shoulder-width, never crossed, never shifting. When seated for long periods he holds a coffee cup with both hands cupped around it — a containment gesture more than a warming one. He does not slouch, even in private; the only documented exception is the kitchen-island lean in the post-Rio-resurrection arc, when he is photographed (panel-level) actually allowing his elbows to take his weight. It is, in context, a sign of relief.

**Speech baseline.** Low register, measured tempo, full sentences. He completes thoughts before opening his mouth — a several-second deliberation gap that reads to strangers as gravity and to his son as a wall. He does not interrupt. He does not raise his voice to be heard over background noise; he lets the room come to him. When tired, his Brooklyn vowels broaden; when professionally engaged, they flatten into a deliberately neutralized cop-radio cadence. The shift between the two is one of the most reliable affect-meters on the subject.

**Eye behavior.** Direct, sustained eye contact in conversation — *too* sustained for many interlocutors; he does not break first. With Miles, eye contact softens and lingers; with Aaron, historically, it became fixed and unblinking. With strangers in a room he sweeps once on entry (door, exits, hands, faces, hands again) and then settles, but his peripheral attention never fully disengages — he will react to a hand moving toward a waistband before he consciously registers it.

**Hands.** Calloused at the base of the thumb (sidearm grip), short clean nails, wedding ring worn even off-duty and never removed. He has a near-unconscious habit of pressing the ring with the pad of his opposite thumb when thinking — a self-soothing tic that began during the Bendis-era estrangement arc and has not retired. In moments of acute strain, the thumb-press becomes a slow rotation of the band.

**Dress.** Off-duty: dark henleys or button-downs, dark jeans, work boots or low boots, a jacket cut long enough to conceal a holster whether or not he is wearing one. Nothing branded, nothing loud. He owns very few clothes and replaces them like-for-like. The wardrobe is itself a behavioral tell: a man who has decided what he is and stopped negotiating with it.

**Movement through space.** Walks slightly slower than the people around him, which paradoxically makes him the center of any group he is in — people calibrate to his pace. Takes the same routes repeatedly; on patrol-era depictions and in civilian flashes, he favors interior sidewalks (against the building line) rather than curb-side. Enters rooms and pauses fractionally inside the threshold before committing — a holdover from training that has fused with character.

---

## II. CALM — THE DOMESTIC REGISTER

Calm Jefferson is the rarest Jefferson, and the most informative, because the defenses are loosened just enough to see the man underneath them.

**At home with Rio.** He becomes physically demonstrative in a way he is with no one else: a hand at the small of her back when passing in the kitchen, his forehead pressed briefly to her temple in greeting, a thumb sweeping her knuckles when their hands rest together on a table. He is the one who refills her coffee without being asked. He laughs — a real laugh, from the chest, three or four beats — almost exclusively at things she says. The Bendis kitchen scenes and the Ahmed-era domestic interludes both establish this: Rio is the only person who reliably penetrates the over-controlled register, and she does it without effort, which is the point.

**At home with Miles.** Even calm, he is in low-grade supervisory mode. He notices the contents of the fridge, the time Miles came in, the schoolbag on the floor, the new sneakers. He comments selectively — usually on the thing Miles least expected him to notice, which is itself a tactic, conscious or not, for maintaining the perception of omniscience that has served him as both cop and father. Calm-state affection toward Miles is expressed as: a hand on the back of the neck (brief, firm, two seconds, released), a quiet "you good?" that requires an actual answer, and a willingness to sit in the same room reading or watching television without speaking. He believes — correctly, by his own values — that this constitutes love. Miles has had to learn to read it.

**Solitary calm.** He cooks (eggs, rice and beans, simple things — Rio's recipes, learned through repetition). He listens to old soul and salsa at low volume, never with words sung along. He reads — non-fiction, history, occasionally the union newsletter. He does not watch sports with the sound on. He cleans his service weapon on Sunday mornings with the unhurried precision of a religious observance.

**Decision-making in calm.** Slow, sequential, conservative. He asks one or two diagnostic questions, lets a silence sit, and then states the decision in a single declarative sentence. He rarely re-opens a calm-state decision; once made, it is filed. This is why his rulings feel disproportionately final to those on the receiving end — he is not deliberating in front of them, he has already finished.

---

## III. LOW-GRADE STRESS — THE PROCEDURAL REGISTER

The first stress threshold is crossed daily — at work, during the news, when Miles is late, when a name from the old neighborhood comes up. The tells are subtle and additive.

**Speech.** Sentences shorten. Contractions disappear ("do not" instead of "don't"). The deliberation gap before speaking lengthens by perhaps a second. Cop cadence creeps into domestic speech, which Rio reads instantly and which annoys her. He calls Miles "Miles" instead of any softer form; when the softening returns ("Miles, man,"), the system is settling.

**Body.** Jaw sets — the masseter visibly tightens, a tell consistent across artists from Pichelli forward. Shoulders rise perhaps half an inch. The ring-thumb gesture activates. He becomes more, not less, still; the calm appearance is increased *vigilance* compressed into reduced motion, and people who know him can tell the difference.

**Schedule.** He takes more shifts. He volunteers for extra hours, reorganizes the garage, fixes things that are not broken. The "longer hours at work" stress response is real and quantifiable in the published timelines — every major Bendis-era domestic strain is preceded by a panel or two of Jefferson coming home late in uniform.

**Eating, sleeping.** Eats less but on schedule (will not skip a meal — discipline overrides appetite loss). Sleeps shorter, wakes earlier, is found in the kitchen at 4 a.m. with coffee and the lights off, looking out the window. Does not turn the lights on, because turning them on would be admitting something.

**Decision habits under low stress.** Rule-bound to a fault. He defaults to procedure even where procedure is suboptimal, because procedure does not require him to access ambivalent material. Asks fewer diagnostic questions; reaches for the categorical answer faster. This is the register in which most of his historically poor decisions about Miles were made — not in rage, but in proceduralism applied to a situation that required improvisation.

---

## IV. ACUTE STRESS — THE THRESHOLD

The second threshold is crossed when the stressor touches one of the pressure points: Aaron, masks, threats to Rio or Miles, or evidence that his past is leaking into his present. The change is observable across a single panel.

**Voice drops a half-step in pitch and slows.** This is counterintuitive — laypeople expect stress to raise the voice. With Jefferson, anger and fear both *lower* and *slow* his speech. The slower he gets, the more dangerous the moment is. The Bendis confrontation with Aaron (*Ultimate Comics: Spider-Man* #3–4) is rendered almost in slow motion at the dialogue level.

**He stops gesturing.** Hands go to his sides, or one hand to his hip (a stance, not a threat). The thumb-on-ring stops; the body has committed to a different posture.

**Eye contact becomes fixed.** Blink rate drops. The "I see you" stare is what he uses when interrogating suspects and what he uses on family members he is about to issue an ultimatum to. The same instrument, indiscriminately deployed, is one of his great relational liabilities — Miles has been on the receiving end of an interrogation stare in his own kitchen and has felt, correctly, that his father was treating him as a problem to be solved.

**He moves closer, not farther.** This is unusual and a strong tell. Many people retreat under acute stress; Jefferson closes distance. With suspects this is intimidation; with family this reads as confrontation but is partly a containment instinct — he is putting himself between the stressor and the household. The bodily logic is "if I am here, it cannot move past me."

**Decision habits.** This is the register in which he issues edicts: *You will not see him. You will not go out. Take that thing off in this house.* The edicts are absolute, declarative, and not negotiable in the moment. They are also, almost always, regretted within twenty-four hours and modified — never retracted, but softened in application. He does not say "I was wrong"; he changes the enforcement.

---

## V. THREAT — THE OPERATIONAL REGISTER

When the situation crosses into direct physical threat, the affective system goes quiet and the trained system takes over. This is the Jefferson colleagues describe as steady, the one Rio married partly because she saw it once and trusted it.

**Breathing.** Diaphragmatic, slow, deliberate — combat breathing he was trained into and has internalized. Two-count in, four-count out. His chest does not rise; his abdomen does.

**Movement economy.** Every motion shortens to its functional minimum. He does not telegraph. Weapon presentation is one motion, not three. He moves people behind him with a single backhanded sweep of the hand — Rio and Miles have both been on the receiving end of this gesture and have learned to comply without question, because the moments in which he uses it are the moments in which compliance matters.

**Speech.** Drops to near-monosyllabic command vocabulary. *Down. Behind me. Stay.* Articles and modifiers disappear. The cop-radio cadence becomes total; the Brooklyn vowels vanish.

**Threat assessment loop.** Continuous, audible only in the way his eyes move — door, hands, hands, window, hands. He is reading a room as a problem in geometry. Anyone with a hand he cannot see is the priority object.

**Use of force.** Disciplined; he is not a man who shoots first, and the published record shows him absorbing escalation before responding — but once he responds, he commits fully. He does not hesitate mid-action. Hesitation, in his frame, kills people. He will, however, drop a draw the instant the threat condition resolves; weapon goes to low ready, then holster, immediately. The hand stays near the grip for an additional thirty seconds or so before falling away.

**Aftermath of threat.** This is one of the most diagnostic windows. He goes briefly, intensely silent — perhaps five minutes of physical presence with no speech, during which he is running an after-action review in his head. Then he asks, in order: *Are you hurt. Are they hurt. Where are the children.* Only after this does he process his own state, which he typically does alone, often in a bathroom, sometimes with his hands braced on the sink. The hands tremble post-incident; he waits them out.

---

## VI. INTIMACY — WHAT HE WILL AND WILL NOT DO

Intimacy is the register in which the over-control is most expensive and the rewards, when he pays the cost, are most visible.

**With Rio.** He is physically open in private — sleeps with an arm across her, wakes when she moves, will lie awake holding her if she has had a hard shift. He does not perform affection in public beyond the small gestures noted above; he does not need to, and she does not need him to. Verbal intimacy is sparser than physical, but specific: he tells her she is right when she is right, he tells her thank you for things most husbands do not name, and on rare occasions — usually after a near-miss at work — he tells her plainly that he would not survive without her. He means it literally; she knows.

**With Miles.** The intimacy ceiling is lower and the cost higher. He can put a hand on his son's shoulder. He can sit in a hospital room overnight without speaking. He can — and this is the great late-arc development — stand in a room where Miles is in the suit and not leave. What he struggles to do is *speak* the love without a barrier. The film-canon doorway monologue is not an aberration; it is the architecture. He can say it when he believes he is not being heard. The Bendis post-reveal conversations (*Spider-Man* #240) are the same structure with a different door: he speaks while looking somewhere else, often out a window, often while doing something with his hands.

**Sexual intimacy.** Not depicted explicitly, but the marriage is consistently rendered as physically warm and present. The absence of any depicted infidelity, drift, or sexual avoidance pattern is itself data; the marriage is a working one.

**With friends and peers.** He does not have close friends in the published record outside the household. He has colleagues he respects, a precinct culture he participates in, a Brooklyn neighborhood that knows him. Intimacy in this layer is shared task and shared territory, not disclosure. He has never, on-panel, told a male peer about Aaron unprompted.

**Tells that intimacy is being attempted.** He sits down — actually sits, instead of standing or pacing. He takes off the jacket. He uses the person's name at the start of a sentence ("Miles, listen —"). He asks a question and waits for the answer without preparing his rebuttal. The waiting is the tell; he is a man who normally has the next sentence ready.

---

## VII. GRIEF — THE PRIVATE REGISTER

Grief is the register he handles worst and most privately. The published record shows two major grief episodes (Aaron, Rio) and several smaller ones (line-of-duty losses, the estrangement period with Miles).

**Phase one: denial through activity.** Immediately following a loss he works. He takes shifts, he fixes things in the apartment, he organizes paperwork. The activity is not avoidance in any conscious sense; it is the only register in which his body knows how to metabolize. He will look exhausted and refuse to stop. Rio used to physically remove tools from his hands.

**Phase two: somatic compression.** Within a few days the body starts to register. He stops eating regular meals. He loses perhaps five to seven pounds, visibly in the face and around the eyes. Sleep collapses into two- or three-hour fragments. He is up before dawn and out walking — long, slow, route-less walks through Brooklyn, often ending up at locations associated with the lost person without his having consciously chosen them.

**Phase three: anger displacement.** This is the dangerous phase, the one in which Spider-Man became the target after Rio's death and Aaron's life became the target of his rejection long before Aaron's death. The grief routes to a categorical enemy and stays there until the system finds something more accurate to do with it.

**Phase four: ritual.** He develops small private observances. He keeps Rio's mug on the shelf in the resurrected timeline as a memory of when it was the only thing of hers he had left. He visits Aaron's grave (in arcs that permit it) on specific dates and stands without speaking. He does not bring flowers; he brings his presence, which in his moral economy is the larger offering.

**Phase five: integration without resolution.** He does not "get over" things. He builds a structure around them and continues to function. The grief becomes a permanent feature of the architecture rather than a passing weather. This is observable in the late-Ahmed and Ziglar runs as a deepening rather than a healing — he is the same man, only with more interior square footage given over to absences.

**Tells in grief.** Quieter than baseline (which is already quiet). Slower. The wedding-ring rotation becomes constant. He looks at middle distance, often through people. He answers questions accurately but offers nothing unprompted. He does not cry in front of others, with the documented exception of Rio's bedside and, in one panel of the post-reveal Bendis arc, in front of Miles — and even then it is one slow exhale and a hand over the eyes, not collapse.

---

## VIII. VICTORY — WHAT HE DOES WITH A WIN

Victory is the register Jefferson handles with the most discomfort, because victory invites self-regard and self-regard is suspect in his moral economy.

**Professional wins.** Closed cases, commendations, promotions. He does not celebrate. He acknowledges, files, returns to work. He will accept a handshake; he will not accept a toast unless it is offered by a superior in front of subordinates, in which case he accepts it as a duty. He tells Rio about the win in passing, often at the end of a longer conversation about her day. He does not tell Miles unless asked, and even then minimizes.

**Family wins.** Miles's report card, Miles's good news, Rio's nursing milestones — these he marks with food. He cooks. He brings something home. He sits at the table longer. The most expansive he becomes in victory is a wide, slow smile and a single hand squeeze on the back of the relevant person's neck. He does not give speeches.

**Moral wins.** When he is proven right — and he often is, in the careful, conservative way he calls things — he does not collect on it. He will not say "I told you." This is partly discipline and partly strategy; he understands, accurately, that the unspoken correctness lands harder than the spoken one. Rio has learned to read the very specific small nod he gives when something he predicted has come true. He is not above the satisfaction; he simply does not externalize it.

**The danger of victory.** He is, against type, slightly less vigilant immediately after a win. The body relaxes a half-degree, the threat scan slows. Skilled antagonists in the published record have not exploited this window, but a surveillance operator would mark it: the safest moment to approach the subject is approximately thirty minutes after he has been told something good.

---

## IX. DEFEAT — WHAT HE DOES WHEN HE LOSES

Defeat — losing a case, losing a person, being proven wrong, having his moral architecture exposed — is the register that produces his worst behavior and his most important growth.

**First-order response.** Stillness. A long silence, sometimes minutes. He does not argue back in the moment of defeat; he absorbs. People mistake this for acceptance. It is not; it is processing under compression.

**Second-order response.** Withdrawal. He leaves the room, often the building. He goes for a walk, drives, or finds a reason to be at the precinct. The household learns to let him go and to expect him back within hours, never more than a day.

**Third-order response.** Re-engagement through act, not speech. He does not return and announce that he was wrong. He returns and does the thing the correction implied. If he was wrong to forbid Miles contact with someone, he does not lift the ban verbally — he is in the room the next time Miles is with that person, and he does not object. The lifting of the rule is enacted, not declared. This is one of his most consistent behavioral signatures across every writer in the canon.

**The badge-on-the-table gesture.** When defeat is total — when he believes he has failed in the role itself — he literalizes it. He has, in multiple arcs, put the badge on a table and stared at it. Sometimes he picks it back up; sometimes Rio picks it up and hands it back. The gesture is not theater; it is the only way he has of representing to himself that the role is conditional on conduct and must be re-earned. It is also a tell that he is in his deepest layer of self-doubt and should not be left alone in it.

**Tells in defeat.** The voice drops further than in stress and stays dropped. The thumb-on-ring becomes thumb-around-ring, the whole hand cupping it. He sleeps either much less or, atypically, much more — twelve-hour nights for two or three days while the system reorganizes. He becomes, briefly, the man Miles least recognizes: smaller, slower, less certain. He does not stay there.

---

## X. SITUATIONAL HABITS — THE GRANULAR LAYER

A surveillance file of any value contains the small recurring things. The following are the subject's documented or strongly inferable habits, indexed by domain:

**Routes.** Favors the same two or three paths between home, the precinct, and Miles's school. Walks more than drives within a fifteen-block radius. Avoids the block where Aaron was last seen alive in the Ultimate continuity; in the 616-integrated continuity, the avoidance has migrated to other associated geographies but the pattern persists.

**Entry to a building.** Pauses inside the threshold. Removes sunglasses immediately, regardless of light. Acknowledges the doorman or building staff by name; remembers their children's names.

**Entry to his own home.** Hangs keys on the same hook every time. Removes the jacket before greeting anyone. Calls out — "Rio, I'm home," or "Miles?" — even if he has reason to believe the apartment is empty. The call-out is partly affection and partly threat assessment (an answer or its absence is data).

**Phones.** Carries two — personal and duty. Personal phone face-down on the table at meals. Will not answer the duty phone at the dinner table unless he has flagged the shift as on-call; this is a discipline Rio enforces and he agrees with.

**Eating.** Eats slowly, finishes his plate, thanks whoever cooked even if it was him. Will not start before everyone is seated. Drinks water with meals, coffee between them, beer occasionally and never more than one in a sitting.

**Driving.** Hands at nine and three, mirrors checked on a regular cadence even on familiar routes. Does not use the horn. Will let an aggressive driver pass without reaction; the only documented exception is when the aggressive driver endangers a pedestrian, at which point the cop emerges and the plate is noted.

**Bars and public spaces.** Sits where he can see the door. Orders the same drink (beer, occasionally a brown spirit on a hard day, one only). Pays cash where possible. Tips well and consistently. Does not stay long.

**With strangers in distress.** Stops. Always. Even off-duty, even tired, even with the family waiting. This is the cleanest behavioral expression of his self-concept — the man he chose to become is the man who does not walk past. Rio has learned to factor an extra fifteen minutes into any joint outing.

**With children.** Softens. The voice loses the cop register entirely. He crouches to their eye level. He asks their names. This is consistent across every depiction and is one of the few registers in which the under-praising habit fully drops; he will tell a child they did something well, plainly, and watch the praise land.

**With his own past, when it appears.** Goes very still


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6: DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

## Subject: Jefferson Davis / Morales

The subject's life, observed across a representative seven-day surveillance window, is one of the most temporally regimented on file outside of active-duty military personnel. The schedule is not imposed by the department — patrol sergeants enjoy considerable latitude — but self-imposed, and the self-imposition is itself diagnostically meaningful (see §3: proceduralism, over-control). The routine is the man. Any disruption of the routine is the most reliable advance indicator of internal disturbance.

---

## 1. The Diurnal Frame

**Wake.** 0515 on duty days, 0600 on rest days. No alarm clock dependency observed in the published record beyond the first ring; subject is awake before the second. Across the Bendis and Ahmed runs, scenes set in the Morales kitchen at "early hour" repeatedly show Jefferson already dressed, already moving, while Rio and Miles are still loading in. This is a man who treats the boundary between sleep and waking as a threshold to be crossed cleanly, not lingered at.

**First fifteen minutes.** Bathroom, splash water (not shower yet — shower is post-PT), shave with a safety razor in front of the medicine-cabinet mirror. The shave is daily and is performed even on rest days. The grooming kit is sparse and military-orderly: razor, brush, single bar of unscented soap, a witch-hazel astringent. He does not own cologne. The face presented to the world is the same face every day.

**PT.** Forty to fifty minutes, six days a week, in the apartment or a nearby precinct gym. Calisthenic-heavy: push-ups, pull-ups on a doorframe bar, weighted carries, kettlebell complexes. No vanity hypertrophy work. The workout is functional — the body of a man who expects to physically restrain another adult human at some point in his shift. Sunday is rest day or a longer walk.

**Breakfast.** Eggs, coffee, occasionally a piece of fruit Rio has put in the bowl. Black coffee, two cups, no sugar. The coffee is not a pleasure ritual; it is a fuel-load procedure, consumed quickly while reading whatever briefing material or local news he has on his phone. Rio's cooking, when she is present, slows him down — one of the few interruptions to his clock he submits to without resistance.

**Departure.** Uniformed shift days, he leaves the apartment between 0645 and 0700. Pat of the hip to confirm sidearm, glance to confirm shield, hand on the doorframe before he steps through — a kinetic ritual repeated thousands of times across the published record, visible in panel after panel. He says the same short phrase to Rio at departure ("I'll call you"); to Miles he says less, often only a nod or a hand on the shoulder. Verbal economy at the threshold is total.

---

## 2. The Workweek

**Shift pattern.** Most of the canon situates him on day-tour (0730–1600) with rotating extensions. During the HYDRA-occupation arc and during high-tempo Spider-Verse incidents, this elongates without complaint. He does not take comp time. Vacation days accrue and are spent reluctantly, usually only when Rio organizes a family trip.

**The commute.** Subway, not personal vehicle, for the majority of the run (the family vehicle is Rio's domain, used for grocery runs and out-of-borough visits). He stands rather than sits on the train even when seats are open, back to a wall when possible, eyes moving. This is not paranoia; it is trained vigilance running at idle. He reads on the train — almost always something procedural or biographical, rarely fiction.

**At the precinct.** Arrives 15–20 minutes before muster. Coffee from the precinct urn (worse than the home coffee; he drinks it without comment). Roll-call posture: upright, attentive, does not banter during briefing but participates in the post-briefing huddle. With subordinates he is the kind of supervisor who explains the why of an order once and expects compliance thereafter; with senior officers he is correct, slightly formal, and unmistakably unbought — the published record shows him repeatedly declining the small corruptions (free meals beyond the customary, fixed tickets for friends-of-friends, the soft favors that lubricate precinct life). This costs him certain promotions and certain friendships, which he accepts as the cost of the architecture.

**On patrol or in supervisory rounds.** He drives the sector car himself when paired with a junior officer, a small dominance/teaching pattern. He knows the businesses on his beat by owner's first name. He stops to talk to the older women on the stoops in a way he does not stop to talk to anyone else in his life — a softer register he reserves for community elders, mirroring how he was likely raised to address them. He is conspicuously present at the schools at dismissal hours when his patrol routes allow it, a behavior that escalates noticeably during periods when Miles is in particular danger.

**Lunch.** Eaten at his desk or in the car. A sandwich Rio has packed, or a halal-cart plate from one of two specific vendors he uses. He does not eat in restaurants during the workday. Lunch is fifteen to twenty minutes, often interrupted, never extended.

**End of shift.** Paperwork completed before leaving. He is the supervisor who stays the extra forty minutes to close out the file rather than push it to the next tour. He changes out of uniform at the precinct on shifts where he is going directly home — the uniform stays in the locker, the off-duty clothes (chinos or jeans, a plain shirt, a zip-up jacket, a Mets or Knicks cap depending on season) are themselves a uniform of a different kind.

**Off-duty carry.** Yes, always, in a hip holster under the jacket. The piece is in a small lockbox at the apartment entryway nightly — a ritual performed before he greets anyone, before he removes his shoes, before any other transition.

---

## 3. The Apartment

**Spatial habits.** The Brooklyn apartment in the published record is not large. Jefferson's territory within it is recognizable: a specific chair at the kitchen table (the one facing the door), a specific corner of the couch, a small section of bedroom dresser-top where the badge, wallet, keys, and phone are laid out each night in the same arrangement. The arrangement is identical morning after morning — surveillance would note that displacement of any item by more than a few inches produces a small re-centering gesture, performed without conscious attention.

**Maintenance behaviors.** He is the one who fixes things. Leaky faucets, sticking doors, electrical outlet plates — small repairs are done immediately and by him, not deferred and not contracted out. The toolbox is organized. This is partly economic and partly a tell: when emotionally overloaded, he gravitates to small fixable physical problems as a regulatory practice. During the estrangement arcs, observed behavior includes extended periods of focused manual work — sanding, repainting, re-caulking — at hours that would not normally be repair hours.

**Cooking.** Limited repertoire, executed competently. Eggs, grilled meats, rice. He does not cook the Puerto Rican food that defines the household's table; that is Rio's domain and he is a respectful diner at it, never an appropriator. On Rio's late shifts at the hospital he cooks for Miles, and the meals on those nights are conspicuously simple — he is not performing fatherhood through food; he is feeding his son.

**Television and media.** Sports (Mets, Knicks, boxing), news (local more than cable), occasional documentaries. He does not binge serialized drama. He falls asleep in the chair during late games and is moved to bed by Rio. He does not consume superhero media of any kind — a continuity-spanning avoidance that should be read as both displacement and a refusal to participate in the cultural celebration of the thing that took his wife the first time and could take his son.

---

## 4. Marriage, Daily Texture

The marriage to Rio is operated, day-to-day, through small parallel rituals more than through extended conversation. Coffee handed over without asking. The pat on the small of her back as he passes behind her at the stove. The phone call from the precinct around 1100 ("just checking") that they both pretend is about logistics. The shared end-of-day fifteen minutes on the couch before the television goes on, where the day is debriefed in shorthand both of them understand.

Disagreements are conducted in low voices and rarely in front of Miles. The published record shows them as a couple that does not perform for their child — affection is real but understated in his presence, and conflict is taken to the bedroom or postponed. Reconciliation after conflict is initiated by Jefferson through action (the coffee, the repair, the standing-in-the-room) more often than through speech; Rio is the one who insists on the verbal closure, and he submits to it because she requires it.

Sexual life is private in the canon and remains so here; what is observable is sustained physical comfort — he reaches for her, she for him, in the small unwatched moments. The intimacy register at home is markedly higher than the intimacy register he displays anywhere else in his life.

During the period of Rio's death and her later return, the apartment's rhythm visibly degrades in her absence (meals reduced to function, the kitchen unused, hours at the precinct extending) and reconstitutes in her presence.
